And a report by the Prince\u2019s Trust, \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.princes-trust.org.uk\/about-the-trust\/research-policies-reports\/slipping-through-the-net\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ESlipping Through the Net\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E (2016) dispels the myth that all young people can navigate the digital world with ease.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMany of us take for granted use of the Internet in our daily lives; staying in touch with family and friends, browsing for business and social purposes, paying bills, banking, transacting, sharing information, studying, playing games, booking events, or finding our way round whether it be online timetables or maps. The list goes on. Increasingly we use the Internet for smart homes and healthcare and the government agenda by degrees is becoming digital by default. For many, this use of the Internet translates into social connections, up-to-date knowledge, convenience, financial discounts, good money management, and improved well-being.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EHowever, for those who don\u2019t have access to a device connected to the Internet, or the skills to use it, or an understanding and awareness of what the digital world has to offer or have a fear of being scammed, it can translate into frustration, a lack of confidence and exclusion from the benefits the Internet has to offer. In the UK, 28% of those aged 60+ are offline with the main barriers to digital inclusion cited being lack of motivation, \u2018too complicated\u2019, and not knowing \u2018where to start\u2019. which provides leadership and services to its members in the Independent Advice Network across Northern Ireland to help ensure accessible advice services, has long recognised the value of digital inclusion as part of its work, and never more so than now in the face of the difficulties faced by vulnerable people applying for Universal Credit, a welfare benefit which is digital by Active Engagement (SAE) project\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, funded by the National Lottery Community Fund.\u0026nbsp; SAE includes the delivery, by trained volunteers, of a 10-12 week Rights4Seniors digital learning course which teaches seniors how to navigate the Internet so they can access trusted information about their rights and entitlements and know how and where to seek free, independent advice. The programme, which is in its sixth year, has been highly successful with an external evaluation stating, \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cblockquote\u003E\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u2019\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe evaluation demonstrates SAE\u2019s significant achievements\u2026 It also demonstrates the \u2018fit\u2019 between the project, and indeed Advice NI\u2019s rights-based digital inclusion work more broadly, in relation to a number of strategic themes including digital inclusion of older people, tackling information poverty, promoting wellbeing and volunteering.\u2019 \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E(p33).\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/em\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\u003C\/blockquote\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWith the current funding coming to an end and keen to both sustain and develop the valuable work of the SAE programme, I began to look across the globe at international practice. I was keen to explore how community based education programmes overseas were addressing digital exclusion among older people in order to gain new perspectives and learning on policy and practice that could be applied in Northern Ireland.\u0026nbsp;\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn 2018, funded by the \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.wcmt.org.uk\/\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWinston Churchill Memorial Trust\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, I travelled to Australia and Japan to explore how digital inclusion learning programmes in both countries were enabling older people to reap the benefits of the Internet, e.g. reducing social isolation, improving independence, financial inclusion and better quality of life. Such research would build on Advice NI\u2019s digital inclusion initiatives by bringing back ideas and knowledge that could inform proposals to implement key policy areas both regionally and across the UK. While there are many excellent digital initiatives in the UK aimed at encouraging older people to go online, they are often short or \u2018taster\u2019 sessions e.g. Silver Surfers Day. Programmes that offer longer term support help build confidence and motivation to ensure that older people are well placed to take advantage of digital systems and processes. This is particularly important as many of our government and other services move online and older people become even more at risk of exclusion.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n","format":"basic_html","processed":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EA I was keen to explore how community based education programmes overseas were addressing digital exclusion among older people in order to gain new perspectives and learning on policy and practice that could be applied in Northern Ireland.\u00a0\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn 2018, funded by the \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.wcmt.org.uk\/\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWinston Churchill Memorial Trust\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, I travelled to Australia and Japan to explore how digital inclusion learning programmes in both countries were enabling older people to reap the benefits of the Internet, e.g. reducing social isolation, improving independence, financial inclusion and better quality of life. Such research would build on Advice NI\u2019s digital inclusion initiatives by bringing back ideas and knowledge that could inform proposals to implement key policy areas both regionally and across the UK. While there are many excellent digital initiatives in the UK aimed at encouraging older people to go online, they are often short or \u2018taster\u2019 sessions e.g. Silver Surfers Day. Programmes that offer longer term support help build confidence and motivation to ensure that older people are well placed to take advantage of digital systems and processes. This is particularly important as many of our government and other services move online and older people become even more at risk of exclusion.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E"},"field_headline":null},"relationships":{"paragraph_type":{"data":{"type":"paragraphs_type--paragraphs_type","id":"82d548fc-dbb2-42ac-8e64-a71ca76a0185"},"links":{"related":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/551e9b9e-ed67-42b7-b71a-bb205d7e730c\/paragraph_type"},"self":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/551e9b9e-ed67-42b7-b71a-bb205d7e730c\/relationships\/paragraph_type"}}}}},{"type":"paragraph--basic","id":"cae145ae-e3e1-4e06-9480-3eded5bbf986","links":{"self":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/cae145ae-e3e1-4e06-9480-3eded5bbf986"}},"attributes":{"drupal_internal__id":11,"drupal_internal__revision_id":143,"langcode":"en","status":true,"created":"2020-02-05T15:44:53+00:00","parent_id":"17","parent_type":"node","parent_field_name":"field_sections","behavior_settings":[],"default_langcode":true,"revision_translation_affected":null,"field_content":{"value":"\u003Cp\u003EThese originally set up in 1972 by the Cabinet Office of Japanese Government, develops and manages the accreditation of \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca who are similar to what in the UK might be termed Internet Champions. To be an accredited Senior Life Adviser, the tutor needs to undergo training developed by NMDA and then pass an exam which has written, practical and presentation elements to it. Advisers are then required to re-validate every 3 years in order to keep their skills up to date.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOnce qualified, a Senior Life Adviser can run classes, charging a fee to the participants or can seek to deliver courses paid for by the local prefecture (council). provides a place for seniors to create their own space and place. The organisation which has a part-time staff member, runs classes, provides a job matching service for older people and supports senior community business entrepreneurship. During my visit, I participated in 3 classes, Braining Training which was playing memory games on the iPads provided; a PC class where participants were making New Year cards; and an English class where we discussed the benefits of the Internet for older people. The IT classes were led by an accredited Senior Life Adviser. On speaking with staff, tutors and participants, it was clear that older people participated in the classes for the social aspect as well as the learning. The classes I attended were well organised, fun and relaxed. During my visit, I participated in 3 classes, Braining Training which was playing memory games on the iPads provided; a PC class where participants were making New Year cards; and an English class where we discussed the benefits of the Internet for older people. in Australia some older people I spoke with, while keen to embrace the digital world, expressed resentment at being \u2018forced\u2019 to go online in order to access services and save money by getting better deals. The Australian government at both federal and state levels has put in place funding initiatives and support to enable organisations working with those who are digitally excluded to build the skills and trust to be able to navigate the Internet.\u0026nbsp; In Japan, many local prefectures (councils) were supporting Non Profit Organisations (NPOs) to run classes and drop-ins to support older people to get online.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EPrior to my Fellowship travels, Universal Credit (UC) was being rolled out across Northern Ireland. UC is a single social security payment which replaces 6 other benefits and is for those who are out of work or on a low income. The application process is entirely digital and involves verifying who you are by scanning and uploading specific identity documents, having an email account and maintaining an online job log search.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ETherefore applying for and maintaining a UC claim requires access to a device connected to the Internet, a certain level of digital literacy, the knowledge required to keep your UC account secure and the confidence to manage an online account.\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EA carried out by IFF Research on behalf of the Department for Work and Pensions found that those who were aged 55 or older and those with long-term health problems had the most difficulty with the digital system. \u201cAge also had a significant impact on the perceived ease of the process\u201d of registering a claim online. (p34)\u0026nbsp; In addition to the difficulties of registering a claim online, 59% of older claimants needed ongoing support to manage their UC digital account (p37).\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThis research did not include UC claimants in Northern Ireland, as the roll out of UC was not completed until December 2018.\u0026nbsp; However, given that Northern Ireland has higher levels of Internet non-users than any other UK region, it can be assumed that these findings are relevant to Northern Ireland also.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n","format":"basic_html","processed":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EHowever in Australia some older people I spoke with, while keen to embrace the digital world, expressed resentment at being \u2018forced\u2019 to go online in order to access services and save money by getting better deals. The Australian government at both federal and state levels has put in place funding initiatives and support to enable organisations working with those who are digitally excluded to build the skills and trust to be able to navigate the Internet.\u00a0 In Japan, many local prefectures (councils) were supporting Non Profit Organisations (NPOs) to run classes and drop-ins to support older people to get online.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EPrior to my Fellowship travels, Universal Credit (UC) was being rolled out across Northern Ireland. UC is a single social security payment which replaces 6 other benefits and is for those who are out of work or on a low income. The application process is entirely digital and involves verifying who you are by scanning and uploading specific identity documents, having an email account and maintaining an online job log search.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ETherefore applying for and maintaining a UC claim requires access to a device connected to the Internet, a certain level of digital literacy, the knowledge required to keep your UC account secure and the confidence to manage an online account.\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EA research report, \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca Japan is termed as having a super-aging population. A key challenge facing Japan is its shrinking economy due to a decrease in its working age population, particularly in rural areas. Many of the community based projects I visited were led by older people and were also providing part-time employment for older people.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EJapan is located along one of the most active earthquake belts in the world and therefore experiences many natural disasters. In 2011, an earthquake followed by tsunami waves resulted in nearly 20,000 deaths. More than half the victims were aged 65+.\u0026nbsp; The Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications in its \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022http:\/\/www.soumu.go.jp\/johotsusintokei\/whitepaper\/eng\/WP2017\/2017-index.html\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWhite Paper 2017\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, has under the theme Data-driven Economy and Social Change, a section on the promotion of Computerization in Disaster Prevention Field in which it has two objectives in relation to \u2018Elderly People\u2019. Both objectives relate to developing systems aimed at quickly and effectively disseminating trusted information to older people via radio, TV and computer tablets. In addition, Japan is exploring how technology can support a super ageing society by developing e-health initiatives, robotics and other assistive devices.\u0026nbsp;\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www8.cao.go.jp\/kourei\/kou-kei\/age_list_all.htm\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Cabinet Office\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E on an annual basis recognises the work and awards a plaque to older individuals and community groups supporting active ageing. Many of these groups are running digital literacy courses and other initiatives to support older people to use technology. I was therefore interested to visit Japan to learn about the programmes and initiatives that were encouraging older people to use digital technology and was particularly keen to find out what was motivating older people to engage in such initiatives.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n","format":"basic_html","processed":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EPeople aged 65 and over account for 28%, i.e. nearly a third, of Japan\u2019s population, with this trend towards an ageing population projected to increase to 40% by 2050. Japan is termed as having a super-aging population. A key challenge facing Japan is its shrinking economy due to a decrease in its working age population, particularly in rural areas. Many of the community based projects I visited were led by older people and were also providing part-time employment for older people.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EJapan is located along one of the most active earthquake belts in the world and therefore experiences many natural disasters. In 2011, an earthquake followed by tsunami waves resulted in nearly 20,000 deaths. More than half the victims were aged 65+.\u00a0 The Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications in its \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022http:\/\/www.soumu.go.jp\/johotsusintokei\/whitepaper\/eng\/WP2017\/2017-index.html\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWhite Paper 2017\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, has under the theme Data-driven Economy and Social Change, a section on the promotion of Computerization in Disaster Prevention Field in which it has two objectives in relation to \u2018Elderly People\u2019. Both objectives relate to developing systems aimed at quickly and effectively disseminating trusted information to older people via radio, TV and computer tablets. In addition, Japan is exploring how technology can support a super ageing society by developing e-health initiatives, robotics and other assistive devices.\u00a0\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www8.cao.go.jp\/kourei\/kou-kei\/age_list_all.htm\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe Cabinet Office\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E on an annual basis recognises the work and awards a plaque to older individuals and community groups supporting active ageing. The Index reported that while the gap had narrowed slightly from the previous year, those aged \u201865 years and older are Australia\u2019s least digitally included age group.\u2019 This is mirrored in the UK, where \u2018since 2011, adults over the age of 65 years have consistently made up the largest proportion of the adult internet non-users.\u2019 (Office for National Statistics, 2017)\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E"},"field_headline":"Australia"},"relationships":{"paragraph_type":{"data":{"type":"paragraphs_type--paragraphs_type","id":"82d548fc-dbb2-42ac-8e64-a71ca76a0185"},"links":{"related":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/9bf374f8-134e-4fc2-93e8-3c9720118f8e\/paragraph_type"},"self":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/9bf374f8-134e-4fc2-93e8-3c9720118f8e\/relationships\/paragraph_type"}}}}},{"type":"paragraph--basic","id":"59dc4de8-06dc-439c-8c08-c95100b9a94e","links":{"self":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/59dc4de8-06dc-439c-8c08-c95100b9a94e"}},"attributes":{"drupal_internal__id":34,"drupal_internal__revision_id":257,"langcode":"en","status":true,"created":"2020-02-07T12:31:18+00:00","parent_id":"35","parent_type":"node","parent_field_name":"field_sections","behavior_settings":[],"default_langcode":true,"revision_translation_affected":null,"field_content":{"value":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThis can be a conundrum; how do you become motivated if you\u2019re not aware of what\u2019s possible? And particularly with regards to the Internet if you\u2019re not a digital native, i.e. you\u2019ve navigated your life to date without it. Participants from Advice NI\u2019s Supporting Active Engagement project gave many different reasons for being motivated to committing to classes with one older man citing; \u2018I heard everyone else talking about asking Google and I wanted to learn how to ask Google too.\u2019\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn Japan, a particular motivation for learning digital skills was \u2018Brain Training\u2019 classes. I attended a class run by the \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.svsoho.gr.jp\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMitaka Senior SOHO Saloon\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E in Tokyo.\u0026nbsp; The instructor started the class with physical exercises by showing different times on a screen at the front of the room. Sitting in our chairs participants were asked to make the time on the clock with our arms.\u0026nbsp; Three o\u2019clock is straightforward, twenty to seven requires some thought! Following the warm up we played a series of memory games on the iPads provided. An instructor led all the games and the class was fun and very sociable.\u0026nbsp; On speaking with participants at the end of the session, the main reasons given for attending were to meet other people as well as exercising the brain. While attendees were learning digital skills, it did not seem to be the primary motivation for attending.\u0026nbsp;\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn both Australia and Japan, a key motivation for learning to use the Internet was for communication purposes, in particular for staying in touch with family and friends. In Uji in Japan, I sat in on a session delivered by accredited Senior Information Life Advisers and on speaking with participants, their motivation for learning new digital skills was clearly driven by social contact. One man who was 90 years old was designing and creating invitations to send out to his peers inviting them to a school class reunion. Another man in his nineties was determined to learn new skills so that he could stay in contact with his granddaughter who was a ballet dancer in London. He was also keen to keep up-to-date with her career by reading online newspapers.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EAgain in Japan, I met \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.japantimes.co.jp\/news\/2018\/03\/13\/national\/kanagawa-computer-programmer-82-recognized-worldwide-efforts-keep-seniors-digitally-engaged\/#.XVWHDm5Fw2w\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMrs Masako Wakamiya\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, who, aged 82, is believed to be the oldest app developer in the world. She created a game which can be downloaded on iTunes. Last year she was invited to the Apple Inc. worldwide developer\u2019s conference.\u0026nbsp; When I asked Mrs Wakamiya what had motivated her to develop such an app she told me that when she retired from banking she developed an interest in digital technology and couldn\u2019t find a game that was of interest to her or her peers so she developed one herself. He was also keen to keep up-to-date with her career by reading online newspapers.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EAgain in Japan, I met \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.japantimes.co.jp\/news\/2018\/03\/13\/national\/kanagawa-computer-programmer-82-recognized-worldwide-efforts-keep-seniors-digitally-engaged\/#.XVWHDm5Fw2w\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EMrs Masako Wakamiya\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, who, aged 82, is believed to be the oldest app developer in the world. She created a game which can be downloaded on iTunes. Last year she was invited to the Apple Inc. worldwide developer\u2019s conference.\u00a0 When I asked Mrs Wakamiya what had motivated her to develop such an app she told me that when she retired from banking she developed an interest in digital technology and couldn\u2019t find a game that was of interest to her or her peers so she developed one herself. She then asked me what gaming apps were available to eighty year olds in Northern Ireland and I had to admit that I didn\u2019t think there were any.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/www.qldseniorsweek.org.au\/\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EQueensland Seniors Week\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E in Brisbane provided opportunities for motivation by offering a raft of different events, many of them offering introductions to technology from shopping to viewing and listening online.\u00a0 People were encouraged to try something new. I went to a session delivered by \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/bsol.asn.au\/frontend\/\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EBrisbane Seniors Online\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, Smart Technology Q\u0026amp;A, where seniors asked tech questions and shared their knowledge. There was much discussion about government services becoming digital by default and resentment at being \u2018forced\u2019 to go online in order to access services and savings. I was also motivated to go to a session on Streaming for Seniors at \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022https:\/\/library.sunshinecoast.qld.gov.au\/Technology\/Tech-Time\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EKawana Library\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, where I learned how to use My Tuner App to stream international radio, my motivation being to learn how to listen to radio stations from home while I was travelling.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\n\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn Takarazuka, Japan, the \u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003Ca href=\u0022http:\/\/www.npoiisa.com\/\u0022\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ENPO International Information Science Association (IISA)\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/a\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E runs classes and seminars for older people to promote the benefits of engaging with IT.\u00a0 In addition, a group of older people are developing a Handyman app which essentially is a Tech for Good project. For a relatively small joining fee (\u00a310) and then an annual fee (\u00a320), the learner has 10-12 visits from a mentor who supports them to become more familiar and confident with using their own device. Founded in 1998, BSOL is entirely volunteer led and has an office in the city, subsidised by Brisbane City Council. It has over 900 members, with an average age of 75, who are supported by 250 volunteers. Requests for digital learning support are processed in the office and then allocated to a volunteer co-ordinator in one of 8 \u2018hubs\u2019 across the city who then \u2018match\u2019 a mentor with the learner in their local area. telecommunications companies in the UK, such as 3 Mobile, EE, Vodafone and O2, are well placed to offer mobile top-up schemes for vulnerable customers which could form part of their Corporate Social Responsibility. One method of implementing this is via organisations who work with vulnerable clients, for example, the independent advice network in Northern Ireland, a network of 70+ community advice organisations, led by Advice NI, who provide free independent advice to vulnerable clients. Similar to initiatives within the utility sector, advisers could provide their most vulnerable clients with a free mobile phone service top-up. This would help them access online services such as their Universal Credit account, paying bills online and money saving apps while maintaining contact with family and friends.\u0026nbsp; In addition, this would help telecommunications companies meet Ofcom\u2019s new rules to better protect consumers; \u2018Communications providers must introduce policies for identifying vulnerable customers \u2013 Responsibility. One method of implementing this is via organisations who work with vulnerable clients, for example, the independent advice network in Northern Ireland, a network of 70+ community advice organisations, led by Advice NI, who provide free independent advice to vulnerable clients. Similar to initiatives within the utility sector, advisers could provide their most vulnerable clients with a free mobile phone service top-up. This would help them access online services such as their Universal Credit account, paying bills online and money saving apps while maintaining contact with family and friends.\u00a0 In addition, this would help telecommunications companies meet Ofcom\u2019s new rules to better protect consumers; \u2018Communications providers must introduce policies for identifying vulnerable customers \u2013 such as people with learning or communication difficulties or those experiencing physical or mental illness or bereavement \u2013 to ensure they are treated fairly.\u2019 See are many models for achieving this. In Advice NI\u2019s Rights4Seniors Digital training, we provide a set of devices for the volunteer tutors to bring to the classes with them. The benefits of this are that everyone is using the same device, therefore making the tutors\u2019 job easier. Also, no one is excluded because they haven\u2019t got a device. The challenge, then is that for those learners who don\u2019t own a device, they can\u2019t practice between sessions. However we have found that often families will club together to purchase a device for their family member.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E\r\n\r\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EIn Australia, similar to the UK, access to an Internet enabled device can be found in libraries. This can be via classes or simply using a drop-in session. However, there is often time stipulations depending on how busy the library is and whether or not you are a member. It also presupposes a certain level of digital knowledge, confidence and skills. Using a mobile office, more commonly known as the DigiVan, the project provides those experiencing, or at risk of, homelessness, and those in social housing, free access to a range of digital services such as WiFi, saving documents to the cloud, setting up email addresses, printing, charging phones, etc. The DigiVan, staffed by volunteers, sets out at night, co-locating with other service providers, supporting vulnerable people on the street and during the day visits social housing complexes where it offers support to older people. The DigiVan\u2019s volunteers can help with accessing online government services and job searches and offer a cup of tea\/coffee. It is now managed by a Steering Group, comprising representatives from different community groups.\u0026nbsp; IDN runs various computer classes for older people, again delivered by Senior Information Life Advisers, adapting the content to meet the changing needs of those aged 65+. For example, they have found that recent retirees are more likely to have used a computer while working than those retiring 10 years ago. When the school shut, due to a declining school aged population, the building was renovated and strengthened to withstand earthquakes before being handed over to the local community. It is now managed by a Steering Group, comprising representatives from different community groups.\u00a0 IDN runs various computer classes for older people, again delivered by Senior Information Life Advisers, adapting the content to meet the changing needs of those aged 65+. For example, they have found that recent retirees are more likely to have used a computer while working than those retiring 10 years ago. Smartphone classes have therefore become more popular and IDN has partnered various telecommunication companies such as DoCoMo to deliver courses and workshops. Schemes such as course participants being able to borrow a device for the duration of the course have proved very successful. IDN also offers courses to enable older people to achieve the Senior Information Life Adviser certification, e.g. Smartphone Tablet Master training.\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/span\u003E\u003C\/p\u003E"},"field_headline":"Inter-Depending Network"},"relationships":{"paragraph_type":{"data":{"type":"paragraphs_type--paragraphs_type","id":"82d548fc-dbb2-42ac-8e64-a71ca76a0185"},"links":{"related":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/31c4cb4c-75cc-4d59-a42d-b5d19dfead1d\/paragraph_type"},"self":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/31c4cb4c-75cc-4d59-a42d-b5d19dfead1d\/relationships\/paragraph_type"}}}}}],"meta":{"omitted":{"detail":"Some resources have been omitted because of insufficient authorization.","links":{"help":{"href":"https:\/\/www.drupal.org\/docs\/8\/modules\/json-api\/filtering#filters-access-control"},"item--eU846zn":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/bd887846-34be-4ace-afdb-ef5b0410b718","meta":{"rel":"item","detail":"The current user is not allowed to GET the selected resource."}},"item--LYVAKLX":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic\/607594c8-75c3-4f31-95e9-8d3094f4d370","meta":{"rel":"item","detail":"The current user is not allowed to GET the selected resource."}}}}},"links":{"self":{"href":"https:\/\/www.digital4seniors.net\/jsonapi\/paragraph\/basic"}}}
